  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6060a81f-9b9b-488f-8c68-6f77255ea4f2'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer5534076778932790050"><i>In the heart of Calcutta lurks a dark mystery. . . .</i><br/><br/>Set in Calcutta in the 1930s, <i>The Midnight Palace</i> begins on a dark night when an English lieutenant fights to save newborn twins Ben and Sheere from an unthinkable threat. Despite monsoon-force rains and terrible danger lurking around every street corner, the young lieutenant manages to get them to safety, but not without</span>
  <span id="freeText5534076778932790050" style="display:none"><i>In the heart of Calcutta lurks a dark mystery. . . .</i><br /><br />Set in Calcutta in the 1930s, <i>The Midnight Palace</i> begins on a dark night when an English lieutenant fights to save newborn twins Ben and Sheere from an unthinkable threat. Despite monsoon-force rains and terrible danger lurking around every street corner, the young lieutenant manages to get them to safety, but not without losing his own life. . . .<br /><br />Years later, on the eve of Ben and Sheere‚Äôs sixteenth birthday, the mysterious threat reenters their lives. This time, it may be impossible to escape. With the help of their brave friends, the twins will have to take a stand against the terror that watches them in the shadows of the night‚Äîand face the most frightening creature in the history of the City of Palaces.<br /></span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">No, and frankly, I wouldn't recommend it. The first book isn't done so well, and contrary to the general consensus, Palacio is far better done. There <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">‚Ä¶more</a></span><span class="fullContent">No, and frankly, I wouldn't recommend it. The first book isn't done so well, and contrary to the general consensus, Palacio is far better done. There are oddities, like it hadn't been drafted well enough prior to diving in, but the writing of it is worth reading the book (much better than Principe)<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5347746853934229210">SPOILER ALERT!<br/><br/>I was very disappointed in this book. I liked Prince of Mist, but this book was not nearly as good (and I didn't think Prince of Mist was great).<br/><br/>For one thing, Grandma does not want anyone telling Sheere that her father was a bad man. But Grandma was the one who, for her whole life, has been telling Sheere that her father is a good man. But she knew his spirit was hunting his children to kill one of them.   <span id="freeText5347746853934229210" style="display:none">SPOILER ALERT!<br /><br />I was very disappointed in this book. I liked Prince of Mist, but this book was not nearly as good (and I didn't think Prince of Mist was great).<br /><br />For one thing, Grandma does not want anyone telling Sheere that her father was a bad man. But Grandma was the one who, for her whole life, has been telling Sheere that her father is a good man. But she knew his spirit was hunting his children to kill one of them. So why did she build him up in Sheere's mind in the first place?<br /><br />How can Ben and Sheere have a mystical connection because they were twins separated at birth? <br /><br />Why did Dad kidnap Ben's friends and tie them up? Why didn't he just kill them all and then kill Ben?<br /><br />Whatever happened to their father's home? Why did he build it so weird? <br /><br />How can they believe one minute that the bad guy knows they are there, because the miniature train starts going around the tracks and has three miniature figures of them inside, and then the next minute feel they are safe enough to go to sleep in separate rooms?<br /><br />And why is it the girl always has to be the one sacrifice herself? <br /><br />The story was not that interesting. It was difficult to follow. Explanations were given in character speech, going on for pages. Couldn't the author find a way to show, not tell? I was actually kind of angry by the end because I really wanted to like the book and find it creepy, like Prince of Mist. I don't understand why VOYA had it as a starred review. <br /><br />The cover art is great, though.<br /><br /><br />Product Description<br />In the heart of Calcutta lurks a dark mystery....<br /><br />Set in Calcutta in the 1930s, The Midnight Palace begins on a dark night when an English lieutenant fights to save newborn twins Ben and Sheere from an unthinkable threat. Despite monsoon-force rains and terrible danger lurking around every street corner, the young lieutenant manages to get them to safety, but not without losing his own life. . . .<br /><br />Years later, on the eve of Ben and Sheere's sixteenth birthday, the mysterious threat reenters their lives. This time, it may be impossible to escape. With the help of their brave friends, the twins will have to take a stand against the terror that watches them in the shadows of the night--and face the most frightening creature in the history of the City of Palaces. </span>

<div id="review_233806344" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/233806344" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2467655-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596119990p2/2467655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/233806344?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/2467655-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer233806344" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9019237781340384477"><b>
  <i>‚ÄúThose places where sadness and misery abound are favoured settings for stories of ghosts and apparitions.‚Äù</i>
</b><br/><br/><br/>I think I can sum up my disappointment in this book in a sentence: <br/>Fantastic ideas that are described in breathtakingly beautiful prose but never explained properly.<br/><br/>This isn‚Äôt going to be a long review because I had the same problems with this book as I did with The Prince of Mist.<br/>There was just not enough explanation and, it might just be me, but I couldn‚Äôt get over that. I‚Äôm trying so</span>
  <span id="freeText9019237781340384477" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>‚ÄúThose places where sadness and misery abound are favoured settings for stories of ghosts and apparitions.‚Äù</i>
</b><br /><br /><br />I think I can sum up my disappointment in this book in a sentence: <br />Fantastic ideas that are described in breathtakingly beautiful prose but never explained properly.<br /><br />This isn‚Äôt going to be a long review because I had the same problems with this book as I did with The Prince of Mist.<br />There was just not enough explanation and, it might just be me, but I couldn‚Äôt get over that. I‚Äôm trying so hard not to delve into spoilers but so many crazy things happened throughout which would have been brilliant (and were certainly unique!) had I just been given a reason as to why they were happening. Without this, I just couldn‚Äôt believe it and I wasn‚Äôt sure that I understood the majority of it. <br />I don‚Äôt mind suspending my disbelief and I love magical realism (it‚Äôs my favourite kind of realism!) but only when what‚Äôs happening makes sense.<br />And, to me anyway, parts of this story didn‚Äôt.<br /><br />But anyway, enough of the negative stuff, let‚Äôs move on to the positives.<br />Because there were tons of things I liked about this book.<br />First up I‚Äôve said it before and I‚Äôve said it again I love love looooove how Mr RZ constructs a sentence. Seriously, his prose is just absolutely stunning.<br />I‚Äôve never been to Calcutta and I don‚Äôt know what the streets look like or how the mist rolls off the Hooghly River but with passages like this: <br /><br /><blockquote><br />‚ÄúThe further he went, the more the station made of glass and steel seemed to melt into the city- a jungle of marble mausoleums blackened by decades of neglect; naked walls once coated in ochre, blue and gold, their colours peeled away by the fury of the monsoon, leaving them blurred and faded, like watercolours dissolving in a pond.‚Äù</blockquote><br /><br />I am instantly transported there. Just gorgeous. <br />I also think that, aforementioned problems aside, Mr RZ definitely knows how to tell a thrilling story. Even though I didn‚Äôt understand a few bits, the ending was so gripping! I‚Äôve said before that I love authors who aren‚Äôt afraid to put their characters (and readers for that matter!) through the ringer and Mr RZ is <i>definitely</i> not afraid to do this. <br /><i>I</i> was afraid, however, because I‚Äôm sure he has a list of all my worst nightmares and just throws them all in to spite me!<br /><br />And then there are his characters. Even though I did get a bit annoyed by the fact that the adults are conveniently absent throughout this whole story, I loved that the children are the focus of the book. With such a colourful cast, it was easy to imagine yourself in that dilapidated house and I liked how his children actually act like children, too. Too often in MG/YA books, the children are impossibly ‚Äòmature‚Äô but in both of the books I‚Äôve read by Mr RZ his characters are still children in the best sense: full of wonder, full of imagination, and members of secret clubs that require a password and only permit special girls to join!<br />My favourite character was Ben with his love for ‚Äúcomplex puns‚Äù and his love for writing plays that are described as <i>‚Äúa phantasmal piece of gibberish in which everyone died, including the stagehands.‚Äù</i><br /><br />Ha!<br /><br />I know I seem to have written a lot without actually saying anything, so I apologise. I enjoyed this book a lot more than I did The Prince of Mist because there seemed to be a lot more depth to the story and the setting was absolutely gorgeous. <br />I‚Äôd definitely recommend this book to people who don‚Äôt need to know every single thing and who can just sit back and enjoy the book for what it is.<br />Just because I‚Äôm not one of those people, doesn‚Äôt mean that you won‚Äôt be. Give it a try just for his prose, if anything!<br /><br />You can read this review and lots of other exciting things on my blog <a href="http://weartheoldcoat.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</span>

  <span id="freeText4519628327774497346" style="display:none"><br />The only reason that I am giving this book a star is because I happen to be a Zafon's fan. But seriously now, Calcutta 1930? no disrespect at all. I hated the Chowbar society members, all of them and I was more sympethtic to Jawahel -villain- but Zafon my man this thing sounded like a movie from Bollywood! I mean a necklace that is split in two, twins, names written backwards. I was waiting for the time when they all sang and the book went musical! <br /><br />I understand that it is meant for teenagers and that you wrote it back in the 1990s. But some things are better left in the past, there is no reason to bring it back again when you have written the angels game, and shadow of the wind! <br /><br /><br />nevertheless any book that is written by Zafon has to have quotes that are epic like, and the ones that have appealed to me are: <br /> <br /><br />there was a time was when i too was young and did all the things young people are expected to do: marry, have children, get into dept,become disappointed and give up the dreams and principles you have always sworn to uphold. In a word, I became old.<br /><br />tactics are the collection of small steps you take to reach a position; strategy, the steps you take when there's nowhere left to go. <br /><br />in the book of life it is perhaps best not to turn back pages.<br /><br />there are two things in life you cannot choose,The first your enemies; the second your family sometimes the difference between them is hard to see. but in the end, time will show you that the cards you have been dealt could always have been worst. life, dear son, is like that first game of chess. by the time you begin to understand how the pieces move, you've already lost. </span>

<div id="review_262310530" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/262310530" />
    <a title="Blair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/272909-blair"><img alt="Blair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1493499323p2/272909.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/262310530?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Blair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Blair" href="/user/show/272909-blair">Blair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780753829134" href="/book/show/11382548-the-midnight-palace">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=read-on-kindle">read-on-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=translated">translated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=macabre-slipstream-weird">macabre-slipstream-weird</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=2012-release">2012-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=kids-and-young-adult">kids-and-young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer262310530" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15635042639223356135">Obsessive followers of my reviews (come on, I know there's loads of you out there) may have noted that back when I reviewed Carlos Ruiz Zaf√≥n's previous YA novel, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7128341.The_Prince_of_Mist__Niebla___1_' title='The Prince of Mist (Niebla, #1) by Carlos Ruiz Zaf√≥n' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Prince of Mist</a>, I said I wasn't going to bother reading this. And it's true, I wasn't. But then I came across a copy in the library, and couldn't resist giving this a try, knowing it wouldn't take me long to read. I'm quite glad I did, as <i>The Midnight Palace</i> is much better than its predecessor.<br/><br/>Like <i>The Prince of Mist</i>, this book was</span>
  <span id="freeText15635042639223356135" style="display:none">Obsessive followers of my reviews (come on, I know there's loads of you out there) may have noted that back when I reviewed Carlos Ruiz Zaf√≥n's previous YA novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7128341.The_Prince_of_Mist__Niebla___1_" title="The Prince of Mist (Niebla, #1) by Carlos Ruiz Zaf√≥n" rel="nofollow noopener">The Prince of Mist</a>, I said I wasn't going to bother reading this. And it's true, I wasn't. But then I came across a copy in the library, and couldn't resist giving this a try, knowing it wouldn't take me long to read. I'm quite glad I did, as <i>The Midnight Palace</i> is much better than its predecessor.<br /><br />Like <i>The Prince of Mist</i>, this book was originally intended for the teen market, but the English translation is clearly being aimed more towards the author's adult fans - again, it comes with a foreword extolling its appeal to readers of all ages. The story starts with Ian, now entering old age, recalling his youth in a children's home in Calcutta - specifically the adventures he enjoyed with a tight-knit group of fellow orphans who called themselves the Chowbar Society. Flashback to 1932, when the seven friends are on the cusp of turning sixteen and leaving the orphanage to make their own ways in the world. An elderly woman arrives at the orphanage with a girl of their age, the intriguing Sheere, and so begins a fantastical rollercoaster ride of an adventure. <br /><br />It's odd that this is supposed to be the second of a trilogy, as other than some elements of fantasy and a seemingly indestructible 'bad guy', it has very little in common with <i>The Prince of Mist</i>. One of the things that annoyed me the most about that book was that it was so vague, completely failing to establish any sense of time or place, and providing very little explanation of the villain's origins. Here, the setting and era of the story are clear from the beginning, and the evil Jawahal is given a backstory that's perhaps <i>too</i> detailed, raising rather a lot of questions. Naturally, since this is YA fiction, it does all get a bit silly - much of the climactic action is really daft, but I didn't exactly expect shining literary brilliance, so that was fine. But I did genuinely like the ending, which seemed oddly melancholy and downbeat for a teen book.<br /><br />A decent little read for fans of the author - atmospheric, exciting and easy to get through in one sitting. Maybe I'll read his next YA translation (due May 2013!) after all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15635042639223356135" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3015588202" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3015588202" />
    <a title="Amy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17792052-amy"><img alt="Amy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1454295058p2/17792052.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3015588202?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/17792052-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17792052-amy?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17792052-amy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17792052-amy?shelf=india">india</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17792052-amy?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17792052-amy?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3015588202" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5522472032970971258">In my yearlong course to read everything of Carlos Ruiz Zafon, I am now into his recent YA novels, each that have a similar theme to them. I loved the quartet/quintent of novels that comprise the Shadow of the Wind/Cemetery of Forgotten Books Series. I also loved Marina. There are four of these novels left, the first is the Prince of Mist. This second one, called the Midnight Palace is also named Niebla #2. But I have no idea who Niebla is, nor how the books might be connected. Even though they </span>
  <span id="freeText5522472032970971258" style="display:none">In my yearlong course to read everything of Carlos Ruiz Zafon, I am now into his recent YA novels, each that have a similar theme to them. I loved the quartet/quintent of novels that comprise the Shadow of the Wind/Cemetery of Forgotten Books Series. I also loved Marina. There are four of these novels left, the first is the Prince of Mist. This second one, called the Midnight Palace is also named Niebla #2. But I have no idea who Niebla is, nor how the books might be connected. Even though they are extremely similar in nature and style. There is a Niebla #3.<br /><br />The Midnight Palace does divert from the usual style as it is set in Calcutta, not Spain. But all the rest of the other elements are there. Children in danger, due to a dark spirit from the past, usually that falls into a familial generation line of past wrongs and misdeeds mixed with mental illness. There are haunted mansions, fire, a child or children sought for death. There are dark tunnels mixed with old legends. It was a dark, misty, poorly constructed kind of a mess. It was hard to follow, and I didn't quite like it. My guess is that the last two novels will resemble more of the same. But I guess we will see. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5522472032970971258" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_174727557" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/174727557" />
    <a title="Monique" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4111021-monique"><img alt="Monique" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1400812804p2/4111021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/174727557?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Monique" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Monique" href="/user/show/4111021-monique">Monique</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11691937-the-midnight-palace">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4111021-monique?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4111021-monique?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4111021-monique?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4111021-monique?shelf=translated">translated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4111021-monique?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4111021-monique?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer174727557" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13926124100177478168">As in all books by Zafon, I loved this one. It had its little quirky <i>um-where'd-that-come-from?</i> moments, but I loved it nonetheless. <br/><br/>The synopsis at <a href='http://www.waterstones.com/waterstonesweb/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Waterstones.com</a> reads as follows: <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>1916, Calcutta. A man pauses for breath outside the ruins of Jheeter's Gate station knowing he has only hours to live. Pursued by assassins, he must ensure the safety of two newborn twins, before disappearing into the night to meet his fate. 1932. Ben and his friends are due to leave the orphanage which has been </i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText13926124100177478168" style="display:none">As in all books by Zafon, I loved this one. It had its little quirky <i>um-where'd-that-come-from?</i> moments, but I loved it nonetheless. <br /><br />The synopsis at <a href="http://www.waterstones.com/waterstonesweb/" rel="nofollow noopener">Waterstones.com</a> reads as follows: <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>1916, Calcutta. A man pauses for breath outside the ruins of Jheeter's Gate station knowing he has only hours to live. Pursued by assassins, he must ensure the safety of two newborn twins, before disappearing into the night to meet his fate. 1932. Ben and his friends are due to leave the orphanage which has been their home for sixteen years. Tonight will be the final meeting of their secret club, in the old ruin they christened The Midnight Palace. Then Ben discovers he has a sister - and together they learn the tragic story of their past, as a shadowy figures lures them to a terrifying showdown in the ruins of Jheeter's Gate station.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>Note: I am not sure if this is a spoiler, though I don't think it really is, but I'm giving you a fair warning anyway, as it has a lot to do with the foundation of the story.</b><br />The first part of this book was a bit shaky, I will have to admit. How many times have we heard of the story of a newborn child (or children, or baby/ies) whose parents were murdered in cold blood by an evil person/being, but which child, by some fortunate twist of fate, is rescued by a benevolent character (who may or may not end up dying anyway), and who leaves such child somewhere (at the doorstep of another benevolent character, maybe?) where the child grows up, shielded from the past and clueless that, upon reaching a certain age, he/she and the evil murderer of his/her parents will resurface? I'm thinking Neil Gaiman's <i>The Graveyard Book</i> and, of course, the most obvious example, J.K. Rowling's <i>Harry Potter</i>. Almost always, a token - <i>something</i> - will be left in the possession of such child that will help in the discovery of his past. Well. Go figure. <br /><b>Okay, it's safe to continue reading the rest of the review now.</b><br /><br />The little "showdown" and "game" towards the end, too, was a bit tacky. If you've been dealing with an apparently invincible enemy, with demonic powers and super-strengths, the "game" would not be something that you'd expect. <br /><br />Notwithstanding the somewhat predictable foundation of the plot and the tacky little parts scattered in the storyline, I enjoyed this book immensely. I've read all of Zafon's previous works, and always, the part which I look forward to - the <i>best</i> thing about his novels, for me - is the suspense. The mystery. The eerie atmosphere that prevails throughout the story. The <i>creepiness</i> of the narrative that makes the hair at the back of my neck stand up on end. Yes, I'm a scaredy-cat, but still. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13926124100177478168" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Mish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4045725-mish"><img alt="Mish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528852904p2/4045725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/228242033?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4045725-mish?shelf=ghost">ghost</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4045725-mish?shelf=translated-fiction">translated-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4045725-mish?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4045725-mish?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4045725-mish?shelf=1990">1990</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4045725-mish?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4045725-mish?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4045725-mish?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer228242033" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16941388859199355376">In all of Carlos Ruiz Zafon books I found his locations to be the highlight. They come alive with rich gothic descriptions. <br/><br/>Prior to The Shadow of the Wind, Carlos wrote a series of young adult books that‚Äôs meant to entice young reader and adults alike. Unlike his first book in the series - The Price of Mist - I found the plot to be on the youngish side, the idea of orphan children forming of a group called the Chowbar Society, where their basic motto is to have each other‚Äôs back, no matter what</span>
  <span id="freeText16941388859199355376" style="display:none">In all of Carlos Ruiz Zafon books I found his locations to be the highlight. They come alive with rich gothic descriptions. <br /><br />Prior to The Shadow of the Wind, Carlos wrote a series of young adult books that‚Äôs meant to entice young reader and adults alike. Unlike his first book in the series - The Price of Mist - I found the plot to be on the youngish side, the idea of orphan children forming of a group called the Chowbar Society, where their basic motto is to have each other‚Äôs back, no matter what, is not original in my opinion. There‚Äôs sufficient proportion of supernatural elements and adventure that I can see would appeal to the 12 - 16 year age group. Looking at it from their eyes, it will certainly enthrall and frightening them. But as an adult, I found the writing and translation fluent, and easy to read but it didn‚Äôt have the desired effect on me.<br /><br />Pursued by an evil villain, two newborn twins are separated at birth. The boy, Ben, is abandoned at an orphanage, while his sister, Sheere, goes to live with her grandmother in hiding. The book primarily focuses on Ben. We get to know him very well, his interaction and friendship with his fellow orphan friends, his nightmares and fears. When it came to Sheere, I didn‚Äôt feel I had formed a strong bond with her. Sheere played a vital role in the finale, yet Carlos didn‚Äôt gave us enough time to get to know her as well, as she only appeared in the final few chapters. I would‚Äôve liked for the chapters to alternate between the twins, to see what Sheere life was like on the run and form a connection with her.<br /><br />The Midnight Palace is my least favourite book of Carlos Ruiz Zafon, but he‚Äôs a magnificent writer, and I‚Äôm a loyal reader of his work. If his books are available to me, I continue to read every single one of them.<br /></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2442794915" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2442794915" />
    <a title="Rae" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35995783-rae"><img alt="Rae" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604709489p2/35995783.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2442794915?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rae" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rae" href="/user/show/35995783-rae">Rae</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35995783-rae?shelf=total-guff">total-guff</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2442794915" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15185739791744350369">*SPOILERS* although to be fair... I don't suggest you bother reading it.<br/><br/>As an admirer of The Shadow of the Wind, I bought pretty much everything Zafon has ever written. Unfortunately, owing to the popularity of his cemetery of forgotten books series, they republished a load of his early YA work with misleadingly stunning packaging.<br/><br/>At first I thought that there must be a translation problem because the writing is so unforgivably explanatory and the dialogue so bad. <br/><br/>Quite frankly, it reads like it</span>
  <span id="freeText15185739791744350369" style="display:none">*SPOILERS* although to be fair... I don't suggest you bother reading it.<br /><br />As an admirer of The Shadow of the Wind, I bought pretty much everything Zafon has ever written. Unfortunately, owing to the popularity of his cemetery of forgotten books series, they republished a load of his early YA work with misleadingly stunning packaging.<br /><br />At first I thought that there must be a translation problem because the writing is so unforgivably explanatory and the dialogue so bad. <br /><br />Quite frankly, it reads like it's been written by a teenager. The darkness shrouds and blankets things, the stars form a canopy, the snow forms a mantle, the sun.... You get the picture. I don't mind a bit of clich√©d weather-describing, but this takes the biscuit.<br /><br />I was going to give it an extra star for having some atmosphere... But the plot made no bloomin' sense. <br /><br />In the dramatic climax, the Big Bad starts what seems to be a sinister game of Deal or No Deal. <br /><br />Oh and the fire monster/ demon /baddie... that's been on fire for 40% of his screentime? That melds himself with the engine of a firey train and storms about in a raging storm of FIRE VENGEANCE... how do you think he is finally defeated? ......... well the protagonist lights a match and......... <br /><br />Also, it's supposed to be Ian that's narrating, but Ian is only present for a minority of the time and seems to be omniscient. <br /><br />The dialogue is dodgy.<br /><br />No character reacts in any kind of realistic way to any situation they meet. They do sometimes explain to the reader in dialogue WHY they aren't behaving in a way befitting of any human being, but I didn't find that helped...<br /><br />The setting is - as always in Zafon novels - the best bit, the mesmerising misty palaces of Calcutta are luscious. Bringing a mystical setting to life is one of his fort√©s and in this early work you can see him developing this skill. <br /><br />Sadly, though, I found the overall effect to be rather pants.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15185739791744350369" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10923110044935000006">I hate it when people say these younger books by Ruiz Zafon aren't as good as The Shadow of the Wind. Of course they're not! But I can totally see where Shadow came from. It's fascinating to see how this wonderful author matured as he wrote his books. He kept getting better and better until genius struck him with Shadow. My only complain about Midnight Palace is that it's set in India, which is as exotic a setting as you can get. But I like Ruiz Zafon's Spanish and French characters. I don't kno</span>
  <span id="freeText10923110044935000006" style="display:none">I hate it when people say these younger books by Ruiz Zafon aren't as good as The Shadow of the Wind. Of course they're not! But I can totally see where Shadow came from. It's fascinating to see how this wonderful author matured as he wrote his books. He kept getting better and better until genius struck him with Shadow. My only complain about Midnight Palace is that it's set in India, which is as exotic a setting as you can get. But I like Ruiz Zafon's Spanish and French characters. I don't know, I kept forgetting this book was set in India because the characters sounded too Spaniard. Still, I loved it. </span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2775161445">

  <span id="freeText3002132497190674754" style="display:none">from Murphy's Library ‚Äî <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.murphyslibrary.com/">http://www.murphyslibrary.com/</a><br /><br />I‚Äôve been presented to Zaf√≥n‚Äôs writing with The Shadow of the Wind, a few years ago. I remember it took me a while to really get into the book, but once I did it, I couldn‚Äôt put the book down until I was done reading it. So when I saw Book it Forward had this ARC open for a tour, I quickly signed up. And I‚Äôm glad I did it, because Zaf√≥n got me hooked again!<br /><br />The Midnight Palace tells us the story of the twins Ben and Sheere. They were newborns when their mother died‚Äîtheir father earlier‚Äî, and they were saved by Peake, a young British lieutenant who loved their mother. A man was after the twins, but Peake managed to deliver them to their grandmother, right before losing his life. Aryami Bose lost her daughter, and she couldn‚Äôt bear losing her grandchildren as well, so she made what she thought it was the best: she separated and hid them.<br /><br />Ben was taken to St. Patrick‚Äôs Orphanage, where he was raised by Mr. Carter with another orphans. On the night Mr. Carter accepted Ben there, a mysteryous man came to talk to him, asking about a baby he may have accepted there‚Äîbut he denied such thing. Mr. Carter followed Aryami‚Äôs instructions and didn‚Äôt tell the man there was a new baby at the orphanage. Sheere was raised by Aryami, but they never stayed too long on the same place, they were always moving and hiding.<br /><br />At the orphanage, Ben had a family, the other orphans. They created what they call The Chowbar Society, kind of a club that met at The Midnight Palace‚Äîand old house‚Äî, there were seven of them, six boys, one girl. On his 16th birthday, he met Sheere and Aryami, and he quickly became friends with Sheere, although he had no idea she was his twin sister. Aryami was there to warn Mr. Carter about the danger Ben‚Äôs into, the boy must run away as soon as possible, because the mysteryous man is coming after him, sooner or later.<br /><br />When Mr. Carter saw himself facing the man again, he was sure Aryami was telling the truth. He told Ben to run, to go after Aryani and Sheere, and that‚Äôs exactly what he did, but he‚Äôs not alone. The Chowbar Society went with him‚Äîthey‚Äôve sworn to protect each other. That‚Äôs when Ben learned the truth about his family and started to find out more about the man who was chasing him and Sheere.<br /><br />The Midnight Palace is an emotional roller coaster. You have to fasten your seat belt and enjoy the ride, because you won‚Äôt see the clock running. Part of the story is told by one of the boy‚Äôs POV, so we get to see Ben through his best friend‚Äôs eyes. I was already aware of Zaf√≥n‚Äôs style because of The Shadow of the Wind, so I kinda saw what was behind the by mystery on this story, but he knows how to tell a story, he knows how to hook you into it. This is the second book on a trilogy, but I must confess I hadn‚Äôt read the previous book, The Prince of Mist, and this was not a problem, once apparently the books stand well by themselves.</span>

<div id="review_567703538" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/567703538" />
    <a title="Mizuki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki"><img alt="Mizuki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368277474p2/16842102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/567703538?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mizuki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mizuki" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki">Mizuki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer567703538" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17986657681122054435">I had just checked Google Translation, and 'Niebla' means 'Mist' in Spanish.<br/><br/>Midnight Palace is Mr. Zafon's Young Adult novel, translated into then published in English after his other YA novel: The Prince of Mist. Unlike the other European settings we'd found in Mr. Zafon's other YA and novels, Midnight Palace took place in the 1930s Calcutta, India. The story centered on a small group of orphans who formed a secret society in order to share knowledge and protect one and other from harm, and a m</span>
  <span id="freeText17986657681122054435" style="display:none">I had just checked Google Translation, and 'Niebla' means 'Mist' in Spanish.<br /><br />Midnight Palace is Mr. Zafon's Young Adult novel, translated into then published in English after his other YA novel: The Prince of Mist. Unlike the other European settings we'd found in Mr. Zafon's other YA and novels, Midnight Palace took place in the 1930s Calcutta, India. The story centered on a small group of orphans who formed a secret society in order to share knowledge and protect one and other from harm, and a mysterious villain who preyed upon a pair of separated twin siblings.<br /><br />The mystery part of the story, like Mr. Zafon's other works, is breathtaking and brilliant, especially the action scenes, the final showdown between our teenage heroes and the villain and the finale of pure white snow over Calcutta (now called Kolkata, means Kali's Temple or Kali's Town in local tongue. By the way, Goddess Kali is Lord Shiva's spouse and also the Goddess of time, death, wrath and bloodshed according to Hindus myth).<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><br />In the middle of the book, I thought the idea of a mad villain wanting to slay the orphaned twins (now both teenagers) of his former friend after 16 long years of time, is quite a weak motivation to drive the villain forward for so long. But surprise! Later it turned out this seemingly weak motivation in fact lays another plot twist, here we must praise the author for his successful planting of suspense.<br /><br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />But sadly I found comparing with the author's other works like The Angel's Game and The Shadow of Wind, in Midnight Palace the characters, their personalities and emotion are quite weak and unsatisfying in comparison. Plus the story is supposed to be the memoir penned by one of the orphans decades after the incident, I found the narration to be very distant from the events and the strong emotions (e.g. fear, surprise, regret; etc) it supposed to inspire in the characters.<br /><br />It's also confusing to see many of the Indian characters went by with English names (only a few of the orphans had Indian names), though it can be partly explained that the orphans were raised in an orphanage ran by an Englishman so their names and behaviors are westernized. Still the more I read the book, the more I felt its characters and description on Calcutta became distant from the Indian people and landscapes I'd seen firsthand during my visits to the country. (Although I must confess I've never visited Calcutta, my knowledge about this city only came from books and TV)<br /><br />Though Mr. Zafon described the landscapes, the weather and different landmarks of the city from time to time in his book; still Calcutta, The City of Palaces, doesn't come vividly to life to me like Barcelona did in The Angel's Game. Despite of these few flaws, I would still recommend this book to Zafon's fans, even though Mr. Zafon clearly isn't at his best.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17986657681122054435" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_163676801" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/163676801" />
    <a title="Courtney" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1739351-courtney"><img alt="Courtney" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1343846657p2/1739351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/163676801?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Courtney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Courtney" href="/user/show/1739351-courtney">Courtney</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061724343" href="/book/show/3372431-el-palacio-de-la-medianoche">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1739351-courtney?shelf=teen-fiction">teen-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1739351-courtney?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1739351-courtney?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1739351-courtney?shelf=misc-supernatural">misc-supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1739351-courtney?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer163676801" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9822285109163389783">This one reads like classic Zafon, of whom I am a big fan. The atmosphere of this book, while set in Calcutta, is not too far off from his later books set in Barcelona (Shadow of the Wind, Angel's Game). It's a bit dreamy, a lot creepy and maybe even a bit magical. The story opens with a British soldier delivering infant twins from imminent danger. The twins are separated by their grandmother to keep them safe from those who might wish them harm. The boy twin, Ben, is raised in an orphanage wher</span>
  <span id="freeText9822285109163389783" style="display:none">This one reads like classic Zafon, of whom I am a big fan. The atmosphere of this book, while set in Calcutta, is not too far off from his later books set in Barcelona (Shadow of the Wind, Angel's Game). It's a bit dreamy, a lot creepy and maybe even a bit magical. The story opens with a British soldier delivering infant twins from imminent danger. The twins are separated by their grandmother to keep them safe from those who might wish them harm. The boy twin, Ben, is raised in an orphanage where our story resumes nearly 16 years later. <br />Ben and his closely-knit group of friends, all orphans, are nearing the end of their days in the orphanage and preparing to move on to the outside world. One night an old woman and her granddaughter arrive and things start to get strange. Slowly but surely, the granddaughter, Seere and Ben realize that they are siblings. Not only that, but that both of the lives appear to be in danger from a mysterious entity that is somehow connected to their later father, a brilliant engineer responsible for building the train system connecting major cities in India. The father, however, passed on in a horrific fire at the grandiose Jheeter's Gate when the train, also carrying 300 orphans, caught fire and destroyed the train, the station and the lives of everyone aboard. Now, a mysterious stranger calling himself Jawahal is after the twins, but Ben and his friends are determined to get to the bottom of the whole affair before anyone gets hurt. <br />I must say, I did figure out the "who dunnit" element long before the book was nearing completion, mainly because it's a totally "Zafon" thing to do. If you've read his stuff and read this, then you'll probably know what I mean. What I did need to figure out was the why, which is what kept me going. The setting for the book is almost a character in and of itself as are several of the locations throughout, including the titular "Midnight Palace". A fun and haunting read.<br /><br />Note: I received the ARC of this book from the publisher. I am not in any way compensated for this review (shucks).</span>
  <a data-text-id="9822285109163389783" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer155195605" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10706269044739267066">You may also read my review here: <a href='http://www.mybookishways.com/2011/03/arc-review-midnight-palace-by-carlos.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Midnight Palace</a> <br/><br/>2 stars<br/>16 year old twins, Ben and Sheere, are reunited after being separated at birth by a terrible set of circumstances that took the life of their mother. Raised in an orphanage in Calcutta, Ben has relied on the support of his close knit group of friends and the kindness of the Headmaster. It‚Äôs been a good life for Ben at the orphanage, but upon the children‚Äôs 16th birthday in 1932, they are considered adults, and are set free to make thei</span>
  <span id="freeText10706269044739267066" style="display:none">You may also read my review here: <a href="http://www.mybookishways.com/2011/03/arc-review-midnight-palace-by-carlos.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Midnight Palace</a> <br /><br />2 stars<br />16 year old twins, Ben and Sheere, are reunited after being separated at birth by a terrible set of circumstances that took the life of their mother. Raised in an orphanage in Calcutta, Ben has relied on the support of his close knit group of friends and the kindness of the Headmaster. It‚Äôs been a good life for Ben at the orphanage, but upon the children‚Äôs 16th birthday in 1932, they are considered adults, and are set free to make their own way. Sheere has been raised by their grandmother and has been moved from city to city, all of her life, in order to avoid a lurking terror that threatens the twins‚Äô very lives. The friends will have to make a stand against this evil, or have no hope for the future. <br /><br />I‚Äôll be honest with you. There were portions of this book that bored me to tears. I did a lot of skimming. That said, there were parts that were interesting, especially concerning Indian history, and I enjoyed the relationships between the friends. However, there was a lot of ‚Äústorytelling‚Äù by a few characters, and as a general rule, I don‚Äôt like this kind of writing. I realize how it can be necessary in certain situations, but most of the time, at least to me, it seems like filler. Also keep in mind this is a Spanish to English translation, and I realize how tough it is to retain nuance and other subtleties in a translation. I can‚Äôt say this book was bad, because it wasn‚Äôt, but it most certainly wasn‚Äôt my cup of tea. I know that Carlos Ruiz Zafon is an extremely popular writer, but I don‚Äôt know if I‚Äôll be seeking out more of his work. The finale of The Midnight Palace just wasn‚Äôt worth the effort for me. </span>

<div id="review_332391695" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/332391695" />
    <a title="Tim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9588897-tim"><img alt="Tim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1337268904p2/9588897.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/332391695?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tim" href="/user/show/9588897-tim">Tim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780753829240" href="/book/show/10625567-the-midnight-palace">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9588897-tim?shelf=general-fiction">general-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer332391695" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2192607863305434561">The only thing I liked about this was the story concept. It's a good supernatural thriller concept, I'm sure it could make for a gripping tale that I wouldn't want to put down.<br/><br/>But not in this form, sadly. I have three major problems with the execution which completely spoiled my involvement in the story.<br/><br/>First, there's no sense of authenticity. The book is set in 1930's Calcutta, but except for street names and place names, you'd never know. It doesn't feel Indian, and it doesn't feel 1930's: whe</span>
  <span id="freeText2192607863305434561" style="display:none">The only thing I liked about this was the story concept. It's a good supernatural thriller concept, I'm sure it could make for a gripping tale that I wouldn't want to put down.<br /><br />But not in this form, sadly. I have three major problems with the execution which completely spoiled my involvement in the story.<br /><br />First, there's no sense of authenticity. The book is set in 1930's Calcutta, but except for street names and place names, you'd never know. It doesn't feel Indian, and it doesn't feel 1930's: where are the cultural nods, where are the technologies that would tie it to a time. And where are the people? This Calcutta feels like a ghost town - it could be anywhere. <br /><br />Second, the authorial voice is inconsistent. There's a conceit that the story is being retold many years later by one of the protagonists, who left the city hours after the story completes and never saw his friends again. But it's all in 3rd person and hops from person to person. How does he know what happened to the others? How would anybody know the omnisicient commentary about the state of mind and awareness of the characters involved?<br /><br />Finally, there's no grounding for the supernatural elements. The world never feels consistent, as readers we don't know what's powers are likely to manifest, so the events feel chaotic and unplanned. That's extremely poor worldbuilding, which robs the story of any tension. <br /><br />A disappointment.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2192607863305434561" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8088845135355119614">After the mediocre Prince of the Mist (very, very YA), CR Zafon returns (in a manner of speaking since the book is from the early 90's predating his two masterpieces but the translation is only 2011) to what we expect from TSoW and TAG; now this book is still YA so we have simple action and relatively predictable plot with a twist and 16 year old heroes and heroines in typical world building that does not question the YA's roles as main leads - hence do not expect the layers and sophistication o</span>
  <span id="freeText8088845135355119614" style="display:none">After the mediocre Prince of the Mist (very, very YA), CR Zafon returns (in a manner of speaking since the book is from the early 90's predating his two masterpieces but the translation is only 2011) to what we expect from TSoW and TAG; now this book is still YA so we have simple action and relatively predictable plot with a twist and 16 year old heroes and heroines in typical world building that does not question the YA's roles as main leads - hence do not expect the layers and sophistication of the two adult novels - but the elements are there: narrative energy, inventiveness, great characters (even as sketches), surprises and the creepy descriptions that justly made the atmosphere of TSoW and TAG so awesome. <br /><br />If you want an introduction to the author and see what the fuss is this book will do since it's short and fast. Highly recommended (again keeping in mind that is still YA so with all the limitations thereof)</span>

<div id="review_526377705" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/526377705" />
    <a title="Yzobelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3745601-yzobelle"><img alt="Yzobelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1397879180p2/3745601.jpg" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/526377705?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yzobelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yzobelle" href="/user/show/3745601-yzobelle">Yzobelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316044745" href="/book/show/12819830-the-midnight-palace">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer526377705" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1473369764228084985">The Master Storyteller did it again! It was by serendipity that I encountered a copy of this book and I am really glad I did!<br/><br/>Intended for teen readers, in The Midnight Palace, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6895030.Carloz_Ruiz_Zafon' title='Carloz Ruiz Zafon' rel='nofollow noopener'>Carloz Ruiz Zafon</a> keeps the style of writing that is sooo uniquely his. As usual, he brings his readers to a web of stories while letting them experience the mix of anguish, horror, and laughter all in one as they get immersed in that web. Even if all his books have this trend of stories within stories, Zafon manages to ma</span>
  <span id="freeText1473369764228084985" style="display:none">The Master Storyteller did it again! It was by serendipity that I encountered a copy of this book and I am really glad I did!<br /><br />Intended for teen readers, in The Midnight Palace, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6895030.Carloz_Ruiz_Zafon" title="Carloz Ruiz Zafon" rel="nofollow noopener">Carloz Ruiz Zafon</a> keeps the style of writing that is sooo uniquely his. As usual, he brings his readers to a web of stories while letting them experience the mix of anguish, horror, and laughter all in one as they get immersed in that web. Even if all his books have this trend of stories within stories, Zafon manages to make each book simply unique and enjoyable. The way he does his development of characters is just so right! The way he shifts the pov of the story is just so in perfect timing that readers would bitterly enjoy the suspense. The way he cuts the stories to bring in another side of the story makes it literally a cliffhanger! ... Gosh! Hasn't he captured me enough yet! My idolizing Zafon has come a bit to the extreme it seems but I must admit, his talent is simply jaw-dropping! How does he do it?! My describing him still pales the real amazement I have for this great author! <br /><br /><i>(A note on the side: Zafon is not like other authors whose plots are just so the same that there's hardly anything marvelous to discover. I would rather not mention such authors here but drama/romance books (always with a military/soldier setting and one main character always dies but the ending is always happy) are typically like that.</i><br /><br />I wonder when (and if!) I will ever reach the saturation point of reading Zafon's books!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1473369764228084985" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

<span id="freeTextContainer12591121775596479236">I'm a little confused about this book. I didn't quite get the reason behind why Ben and Sheere were such a target. It was explained in the book, but I thought the reasoning was a bit simplistic and didn't really make sense. But then, maybe the reasoning was complex and over my head. Or maybe, it was lost in translation.<br/><br/>Another thing that I questioned was the characters' names. The setting is Calcutta and several of the main characters' names were English. Ben, Ian, Isabella. Mind you, it was eas</span>
  <span id="freeText12591121775596479236" style="display:none">I'm a little confused about this book. I didn't quite get the reason behind why Ben and Sheere were such a target. It was explained in the book, but I thought the reasoning was a bit simplistic and didn't really make sense. But then, maybe the reasoning was complex and over my head. Or maybe, it was lost in translation.<br /><br />Another thing that I questioned was the characters' names. The setting is Calcutta and several of the main characters' names were English. Ben, Ian, Isabella. Mind you, it was easier to follow the story with the simple names and it is Young Adult.<br /><br />As for the story, I did enjoy it when I set aside my grumblings. I liked the characters and their relationship to each other. It was short and sweet, and the descriptions allowed me to paint the pictures in my mind.<br /><br />The narration by Jonathan Davis was very good. I enjoyed his characterizations with various accents. You could hear the evil of Jawahal in his voice. My only complaint was that there were no breaks between chapters to warn you of a change. It was one sentence after another, in spite of a switch in location or character. That may have happened in editting, so I won't blame Jonathan Davis for that.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12591121775596479236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer1130839755336491138">As always, Zafon is a masterful storyteller and from the very first sentence I was entranced. His lyric prose alone is reason enough to read his works but, in this particular story, he seems to shine with a youth orientated plot of mystery, adventure and suspense all rolled together. Zafon has this ability to capture the world around him with such unique and realistic descriptions that it makes you feel like you have dropped into the middle of this world he has created ‚Äì both the good parts of h</span>
  <span id="freeText1130839755336491138" style="display:none">As always, Zafon is a masterful storyteller and from the very first sentence I was entranced. His lyric prose alone is reason enough to read his works but, in this particular story, he seems to shine with a youth orientated plot of mystery, adventure and suspense all rolled together. Zafon has this ability to capture the world around him with such unique and realistic descriptions that it makes you feel like you have dropped into the middle of this world he has created ‚Äì both the good parts of his world and the darker, more sinister ones. Although it‚Äôs been on my TBR shelf for ages, I had not yet read the first in this series but when I received the galley proof, I jumped at the chance to read it and had no problem following the story and characters. The book although listed in some places as juvenile really is for the YA audience. The word choices, grammar usage and content are not for the younger set and most would get discouraged and give up just a few pages in. Older and advanced readers might want to give it a try but I think the book would be better aimed at the high school set.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1130839755336491138" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3277797810" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3277797810" />
    <a title="Marija Andreeva" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25876620-marija-andreeva"><img alt="Marija Andreeva" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598997328p2/25876620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3277797810?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marija Andreeva" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marija Andreeva" href="/user/show/25876620-marija-andreeva">Marija Andreeva</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25876620-marija-andreeva?shelf=easy-reads">easy-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3277797810" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15664258397218872920">I like Zafon. And this book started well, It went like this: 4 stars, then it decreased to 3, at times it was 1 star, so the final judgement is 2.5.<br/><br/>It is written well, easy to read, and it has interesting underlying topic (duality in a man: good vs evil), but as it approaches its end it gets too entangled and it makes the reader to lose interest in what is going on or what will happen to the characters. Supernatural is okay, but it needs to be done with taste and good structure, and I feel like </span>
  <span id="freeText15664258397218872920" style="display:none">I like Zafon. And this book started well, It went like this: 4 stars, then it decreased to 3, at times it was 1 star, so the final judgement is 2.5.<br /><br />It is written well, easy to read, and it has interesting underlying topic (duality in a man: good vs evil), but as it approaches its end it gets too entangled and it makes the reader to lose interest in what is going on or what will happen to the characters. Supernatural is okay, but it needs to be done with taste and good structure, and I feel like Zafon lost control over the story, it just kept getting more and more absurd. <br /><br />It's a pity, because it has potential.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15664258397218872920" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FVkvEf8x0WZHW/PuEEJm8+u0/gPLxW1PAXhd7Pl9lKNrOjD90/6ScBxgZSBQMWsxaFZ8aaYxX6lRMgWolfQH8A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }
